\section{Final Closure: From Converged PDE Observables to CKM Data}

\section{Definition of physical observables}

Let:
\[
(W_2, m_*, g_{\rm eff})_{\rm num}(N,t)
\]
be numerical outputs.

Define physical values as:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_2, m_*, g_{\rm eff})_{\rm phys}
=
\lim_{N\to\infty,\; t\to\infty}
(W_2, m_*, g_{\rm eff})_{\rm num}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final anisotropy coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z_{\rm cub}^{\rm phys}
=
-\frac{g_{\rm eff}^2}{144\pi m_*^3}
\,W_2.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Mapping to mixing scale}

Define overlap scale:

\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{ij}
\sim
\exp(-m_* d_{ij}).
\end{equation}

Metric deformation:

\begin{equation}
d_{ij}^2
=
(\delta_{ab} + \epsilon Q_{ab}) \Delta x^a \Delta x^b.
\end{equation}

Thus:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\Lambda_{ij}}{\Lambda_{kl}}
\sim
\exp\bigl(-m_* (d_{ij}-d_{kl})\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

\section{CKM identification}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{ij}| \propto \Lambda_{ij}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{|V_{us}|}{|V_{cb}|}
\sim
\exp\bigl(-m_* (d_{12}-d_{23})\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Numerical comparison target}

Experimental values:

\begin{align}
|V_{us}| &\approx 0.22,\\
|V_{cb}| &\approx 0.04,\\
|V_{ub}| &\approx 0.003.
\end{align}

Thus:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\log \frac{|V_{us}|}{|V_{cb}|}
\approx \log(5.5)\approx 1.7.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final condition}

TECT must reproduce:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_* (d_{23}-d_{12}) \approx 1.7.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{CKM hierarchy reduces to a geometric length difference condition.}
}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Numerical Audit of the Reduced Shell PDE}

\section{Reduced PDE that was actually evolved}

The numerically evolved reduced shell model was
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \Psi
=
\left[
\varepsilon-(|k|^2-q_0^2)^2+\eta\,P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k)
\right]\Psi
-
g|\Psi|^2\Psi
-
h|\Psi|^4\Psi,
\end{equation}
implemented spectrally in Fourier space, with a BCC-seeded initial condition.

The parameters used in the converged run were
\begin{equation}
q_0=\sqrt{2},
\qquad
\varepsilon=0.9,
\qquad
\eta=0.03,
\qquad
g=1.0,
\qquad
h=0.2.
\end{equation}

\section{Observed shell amplitudes}

Let \(A_\alpha\) denote the Fourier amplitudes on the 12 BCC shell directions.
In the converged \(N=28\) run, the measured shell amplitudes were numerically of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(A_1,\dots,A_{12})
\approx
(0,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0.885682,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0,\ 0).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the attractor is not the intended equal-amplitude BCC shell branch.
It is a one-patch branch.

\section{Converged observables of the reduced branch}

Even though the attractor is not the intended BCC branch, the reduced-branch observables themselves do converge.

For the runs \(N=24\) and \(N=28\), the extracted values were:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_2(24)=0.19610816770267134,
\qquad
W_2(28)=0.19610808588984538,
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_*(24)=1.0151684407720902,
\qquad
m_*(28)=1.0151684111201817,
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_{\rm eff}(24)=1.3137731842582538,
\qquad
g_{\rm eff}(28)=1.3137731760709939.
}
\end{equation}

The resulting cubic coefficient was

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z_{\rm cub}(24)=-7.151708082385493\times 10^{-4},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z_{\rm cub}(28)=-7.151705636363020\times 10^{-4}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Convergence check}

The \(24\to 28\) differences are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|W_2(28)-W_2(24)|=8.18\times 10^{-8},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|m_*(28)-m_*(24)|=2.97\times 10^{-8},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|g_{\rm eff}(28)-g_{\rm eff}(24)|=8.19\times 10^{-9},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|Z_{\rm cub}(28)-Z_{\rm cub}(24)|=2.45\times 10^{-10}.
}
\end{equation}

So these reduced-branch observables are numerically stable.

\section{What is proved and what is not}

The following statement is numerically supported for the reduced scalar shell PDE:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The reduced model admits a converged anisotropic branch with }
W_2>0,\quad Z_{\rm cub}<0.
}
\end{equation}

However, the following stronger statement is \emph{not} yet established:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The intended 12-patch BCC branch of the full }(\Psi,X_i^{\,a})\text{ PDE has been numerically realized.}
}
\end{equation}

The reason is simple:
the converged shell amplitudes collapse to one dominant patch, rather than remaining distributed over the 12 BCC directions.

\section{Honest diagnosis}

Therefore the current numerical status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Reduced branch actual values: extracted.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Intended BCC actual branch: not yet closed.}
}
\end{equation}

The obstruction is not the evaluation of
\[
W_2,\quad m_*,\quad g_{\rm eff},
\]
but the absence of a dynamically BCC-preserving coupling strong enough to prevent shell collapse.

\section{Nonredundant next step}

The next step is not to rerun the same scalar PDE.
It is to promote the dynamics to a shell-amplitude system with explicit inter-patch coupling inherited from the \(X_i^{\,a}\)-sector.

A minimal honest form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
\Bigl(\sigma_0+\eta P_2^\alpha\Bigr)A_\alpha
-u|A_\alpha|^2A_\alpha
-v\Bigl(\sum_\beta |A_\beta|^2\Bigr)A_\alpha
-\kappa\Bigl(\sum_\beta M_{\alpha\beta}|A_\beta|^2\Bigr)A_\alpha,
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
P_2^\alpha:=P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha),
\qquad
M_{\alpha\beta}\sim(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2,
\end{equation}
and \(\kappa\) encodes the shell-locking / family-locking coupling generated by the \(X\)-sector.

This is the minimal promotion capable of distinguishing:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{one-patch branch}
\quad \text{vs.} \quad
\text{true 12-patch BCC branch}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

A direct numerical evolution of the reduced scalar shell PDE was carried out with a BCC-seeded initial condition.

The extracted converged reduced-branch values are:
\[
W_2 \approx 0.19610809,
\qquad
m_* \approx 1.01516841,
\qquad
g_{\rm eff} \approx 1.31377318,
\]
which imply
\[
\boxed{
Z_{\rm cub}\approx -7.1517056\times 10^{-4}.
}
\]

These values are numerically stable under the \(N=24\to 28\) refinement:
\[
|W_2(28)-W_2(24)|\sim 10^{-8},
\quad
|m_*(28)-m_*(24)|\sim 10^{-8},
\quad
|g_{\rm eff}(28)-g_{\rm eff}(24)|\sim 10^{-9},
\]
and
\[
|Z_{\rm cub}(28)-Z_{\rm cub}(24)|\sim 10^{-10}.
\]

However, the converged shell amplitudes collapse to a one-patch state rather than an equal-amplitude 12-direction BCC shell.
Therefore these are \emph{not} yet the actual intended BCC-branch values of the full TECT system.

So the honest status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{reduced-branch actual values: yes,}
\qquad
\text{intended full-BCC actual branch: not yet.}
}
\]

The nonredundant next step is to upgrade the dynamics from the scalar shell PDE to an explicitly inter-patch-coupled shell-amplitude system inherited from the \(X_i^{\,a}\) sector, because only that can decide whether the true full TECT branch stabilizes the 12-patch BCC state.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal 12-Patch Shell-Amplitude System Induced by the Class II \texorpdfstring{$X_i^{\,a}$}{X} Sector}

\section{Goal}

The reduced scalar shell PDE was sufficient to extract a converged anisotropic branch,
but that branch collapsed to a one-patch state rather than the intended 12-direction BCC shell.
Therefore the next nonredundant step is to derive the \emph{inter-patch-coupled} shell-amplitude system
that is actually induced by the Class II mediator \(X_i^{\,a}\).

The purpose of this section is to derive:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Psi, X_i^{\,a})
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}[A_1,\dots,A_{12}]
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
-\frac{\partial \mathcal F_{\rm shell}}{\partial \overline{A_\alpha}},
}
\end{equation}

and then obtain a sharp energetic criterion distinguishing the one-patch branch
from the equal-amplitude 12-patch BCC branch.

\section{Shell ansatz on the BCC star}

Let the 12 BCC shell directions be
\[
\hat k_\alpha \in
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,\pm1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\},
\qquad
\alpha=1,\dots,12.
\]

Near the finite-\(q_0\) instability, write the shell truncation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x,t)
=
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}
A_\alpha(t)\,e^{i q_0 \hat k_\alpha\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:shell_ansatz}
\end{equation}

Define the shell intensities
\[
r_\alpha:=|A_\alpha|^2.
\]

\section{Class II induced shell tensor}

From the already-derived Class II heavy-mediator theorem, integrating out \(X_i^{\,a}\) produces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^{\,b}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a \mathcal C_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\label{eq:dN_general_main}
\end{equation}

Its shell-relevant decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^{3}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j+\cdots,
\label{eq:dN3_main}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^{1}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
\Bigl(
B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
-
C\,\hat n_i e_{2j}
\Bigr)+\cdots,
\label{eq:dN1_main}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^{2}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
\Bigl(
B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}
+
C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
\Bigr)+\cdots,
\label{eq:dN2_main}
\end{equation}
where \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\) is an orthonormal frame adapted to the anisotropy axis.

\section{Patchwise shell couplings induced by \texorpdfstring{$\delta N_{ij}^{\,b}$}{dN}}

For each shell direction \(\hat k_\alpha\), define
\begin{equation}
c_\alpha:=\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
t_{\alpha 1}:=e_1\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
t_{\alpha 2}:=e_2\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha.
\end{equation}

Projecting \(\delta N_{ij}^{\,b}\) onto shell patch \(\alpha\) gives
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,b}
:=
q_0^2\,\hat k_{\alpha i}\hat k_{\alpha j}\,\delta N_{ij}^{\,b}.
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:dN3_main}--\eqref{eq:dN2_main}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,3}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,q_0^2\,A\,c_\alpha^2,
}
\label{eq:Gamma3_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,1}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,q_0^2\,c_\alpha
\bigl(B\,t_{\alpha1}-C\,t_{\alpha2}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:Gamma1_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,2}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,q_0^2\,c_\alpha
\bigl(B\,t_{\alpha2}+C\,t_{\alpha1}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Gamma2_alpha}
\end{equation}

These are the exact patchwise shell couplings inherited from the Class II tensor.

\section{Linear growth rates}

The shell-projected quadratic part defines patchwise growth rates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_\alpha
=
\sigma_0
+
\eta\,P_2(c_\alpha)
+
\delta \sigma_\alpha,
}
\label{eq:sigma_alpha_def}
\end{equation}
where the Class II correction has the form
\begin{equation}
\delta \sigma_\alpha
=
\sum_{b=1}^3 \overline{s_b}\,\Gamma_\alpha^{\,b},
\end{equation}
with \(\overline{s_b}\) the heavy shell-adapted background in the internal channel \(b\).

Thus \(\sigma_\alpha\) is no longer a scalar-shell quantity only:
it is explicitly patch-dependent through the \(X\)-sector.

\section{Quartic matrix induced by integrating out the heavy shell mediator}

The same shell couplings induce a quartic inter-patch interaction after the heavy mediator is eliminated.
At leading order, this takes the universal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-
\sum_{b=1}^3 \chi_b\,\Gamma_\alpha^{\,b}\Gamma_\beta^{\,b},
\qquad
\chi_b>0,
}
\label{eq:UX_rankone}
\end{equation}
where \(\chi_b\) is the positive susceptibility of the heavy shell mediator in channel \(b\).

Hence the total quartic matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(0)}+U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)},
}
\label{eq:Utotal}
\end{equation}
with \(U^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}\) the quartic matrix already present in the scalar shell truncation.

\section{Explicit angular form of the \texorpdfstring{$X$}{X}-induced quartic matrix}

Using \eqref{eq:Gamma3_alpha}--\eqref{eq:Gamma2_alpha}, the \(b=3\) channel gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X,3)}
=
-
\chi_3
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
A^2\,c_\alpha^2 c_\beta^2.
}
\label{eq:UX3}
\end{equation}

For the \(b=1,2\) channels,
\begin{align}
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,1}\Gamma_\beta^{\,1}
+
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,2}\Gamma_\beta^{\,2}
&=
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
c_\alpha c_\beta (B^2+C^2)
\left(
t_{\alpha1}t_{\beta1}+t_{\alpha2}t_{\beta2}
\right)
\nonumber\\
&=
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
c_\alpha c_\beta (B^2+C^2)
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta
-
c_\alpha c_\beta
\right).
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X,\perp)}
=
-
\chi_\perp
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
(B^2+C^2)\,
c_\alpha c_\beta
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta
-
c_\alpha c_\beta
\right),
}
\label{eq:UXperp}
\end{equation}
where \(\chi_\perp:=\chi_1=\chi_2\) in the symmetric transverse sector.

Combining \eqref{eq:UX3} and \eqref{eq:UXperp},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-
\Lambda_A\,c_\alpha^2 c_\beta^2
-
\Lambda_{BC}\,c_\alpha c_\beta
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta
-
c_\alpha c_\beta
\right),
}
\label{eq:UX_final}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_A
:=
\chi_3
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
A^2,
\qquad
\Lambda_{BC}
:=
\chi_\perp
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
(B^2+C^2).
\end{equation}

This is the minimal explicit angular quartic matrix that the scalar shell PDE was missing.

\section{Shell free energy and amplitude equations}

To quartic order, the shell free energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}[A]
=
-\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}\sigma_\alpha r_\alpha
+
\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta=1}^{12}
U_{\alpha\beta}\,r_\alpha r_\beta
+
O(A^6).
}
\label{eq:F_shell_main}
\end{equation}

The corresponding gradient-flow dynamics is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
\left(
\sigma_\alpha
-
\sum_{\beta=1}^{12}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\beta
\right)A_\alpha
+
O(A^5).
}
\label{eq:Aalpha_flow}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal 12-patch coupled shell-amplitude system induced by the Class II sector.

\section{Exact BCC angular classes}

For the BCC star, the pairwise angular invariant
\[
M_{\alpha\beta}:=(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2
\]
takes only the values
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\alpha\beta}\in\{1,\,0,\,1/4\}.
}
\end{equation}

For fixed \(\alpha\), the class counts are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{self: }1,
\qquad
\text{opposite: }1,
\qquad
\text{orthogonal: }2,
\qquad
\text{oblique: }8.
}
\label{eq:BCC_class_counts}
\end{equation}

Therefore a BCC-symmetric quartic matrix is specified by four numbers:
\begin{equation}
U_d:=U_{\alpha\alpha},
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}:=U_{\alpha\bar\alpha},
\qquad
U_\perp:=U_{\alpha\beta}\ \ (M_{\alpha\beta}=0),
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}:=U_{\alpha\beta}\ \ (M_{\alpha\beta}=1/4).
\end{equation}

The corresponding row sum is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R
=
U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl}.
}
\label{eq:row_sum_R}
\end{equation}

\section{One-patch branch vs. equal-amplitude 12-patch branch}

Assume first the symmetric case \(\sigma_\alpha=\sigma>0\).

\subsection{One-patch branch}

If only one amplitude is nonzero,
\[
r_{\alpha_0}=r,\qquad r_{\beta\neq\alpha_0}=0,
\]
then minimization of \eqref{eq:F_shell_main} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm 1patch}=\frac{\sigma}{U_d},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}
=
-\frac{\sigma^2}{2U_d}.
}
\label{eq:F_1patch}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Equal-amplitude 12-patch BCC branch}

If all 12 amplitudes are equal,
\[
r_\alpha=r_{\rm BCC}\qquad (\forall \alpha),
\]
then \eqref{eq:Aalpha_flow} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm BCC}
=
\frac{\sigma}{R},
}
\label{eq:r_BCC}
\end{equation}
and the shell free energy becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}
=
-6\,\frac{\sigma^2}{R}.
}
\label{eq:F_BCC}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Sharp energetic criterion}

Comparing \eqref{eq:F_1patch} and \eqref{eq:F_BCC}, the equal-amplitude 12-patch BCC branch beats the one-patch branch if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}<\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
R<12U_d.
}
\label{eq:BCC_vs_1patch_criterion}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:row_sum_R}, this is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl}<11U_d.
}
\label{eq:BCC_vs_1patch_class}
\end{equation}

This is the exact minimal criterion distinguishing true BCC stabilization
from one-patch collapse.

\section{Why the reduced scalar shell PDE collapsed}

The reduced scalar shell PDE effectively omitted the class-dependent quartic matrix \(U^{(X)}_{\alpha\beta}\).
As a result, the dynamical competition was controlled only by the scalar shell saturation,
which numerically selected a single winning patch.

By contrast, the Class II \(X\)-sector produces the explicit angular quartic matrix \eqref{eq:UX_final},
which modifies the class couplings
\[
U_d,\quad U_{\rm opp},\quad U_\perp,\quad U_{\rm obl}
\]
differently.
Therefore it is precisely the missing ingredient capable of changing the sign of
\[
R-12U_d,
\]
and hence capable of stabilizing the true 12-patch BCC branch.

\section{What is proved and what is not}

What is now structurally closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the minimal inter-patch shell-amplitude system induced by }X_i^{\,a}
\text{ is explicitly derived.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the exact energetic criterion separating one-patch collapse from true BCC stabilization is }
R<12U_d.
}
\end{equation}

What is not yet numerically closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual values of }
U_d,\ U_{\rm opp},\ U_\perp,\ U_{\rm obl}
\text{ for the intended branch.}
}
\end{equation}

These still must be evaluated from the explicit coefficients
\[
\Lambda_A,\qquad \Lambda_{BC},\qquad U_{\alpha\beta}^{(0)}.
\]

\section{Nonredundant next step}

The next step is now unique.

One must insert the 12 exact BCC directions into \eqref{eq:UX_final},
compute the four class couplings
\[
U_d,\quad U_{\rm opp},\quad U_\perp,\quad U_{\rm obl},
\]
and test the sign of
\[
\boxed{
R-12U_d.
}
\]

If
\[
R-12U_d<0,
\]
then the true intended BCC branch is energetically preferred over the one-patch collapse.
If
\[
R-12U_d>0,
\]
then the intended BCC branch is not stabilized by the current minimal Class II data,
and stronger or additional inter-patch couplings are required.

\section{Final Summary}

The reduced scalar shell PDE collapsed to a one-patch branch because it lacked an explicit class-dependent inter-patch quartic matrix.

Starting from the Class II mediator
\[
\delta N_{ij}^{\,b}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m^a\mathcal C_{ij}^{ab},
\]
and projecting onto the 12 BCC shell directions
\[
\hat k_\alpha,
\]
one obtains the patch couplings
\[
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,3}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2 A\,c_\alpha^2,
\]
\[
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,1}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2 c_\alpha(B t_{\alpha1}-C t_{\alpha2}),
\]
\[
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,2}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2 c_\alpha(B t_{\alpha2}+C t_{\alpha1}),
\]
where
\[
c_\alpha=\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
t_{\alpha a}=e_a\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha.
\]

Integrating out the heavy shell mediator induces the quartic inter-patch matrix
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-
\sum_{b=1}^3 \chi_b\,\Gamma_\alpha^{\,b}\Gamma_\beta^{\,b},
\]
namely
\[
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-
\Lambda_A\,c_\alpha^2 c_\beta^2
-
\Lambda_{BC}\,c_\alpha c_\beta
\bigl(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta
-
c_\alpha c_\beta
\bigr).
}
\]

Thus the minimal shell free energy is
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}
=
-\sum_\alpha \sigma_\alpha |A_\alpha|^2
+
\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta}U_{\alpha\beta}|A_\alpha|^2|A_\beta|^2,
\]
with gradient flow
\[
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
\left(
\sigma_\alpha-\sum_\beta U_{\alpha\beta}|A_\beta|^2
\right)A_\alpha.
\]

For the BCC star, the quartic matrix has four angular classes:
\[
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl},
\]
with row sum
\[
R=U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl}.
\]

The one-patch branch has energy
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}=-\frac{\sigma^2}{2U_d},
\]
while the equal-amplitude 12-patch BCC branch has energy
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}=-6\frac{\sigma^2}{R}.
\]

Hence the exact sharp criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}<\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
R<12U_d.
}
\]

Therefore the true intended BCC branch is stabilized if and only if the class-dependent \(X\)-induced quartic matrix lowers the mixed-coupling row sum enough to satisfy
\[
\boxed{
U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl}<11U_d.
}
\]

The next nonredundant step is to evaluate these four class couplings explicitly from the 12 BCC directions and the Class II coefficients \(\Lambda_A,\Lambda_{BC},U^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Angular Evaluation of the Class II Inter-Patch Quartic Matrix on the 12 BCC Directions}

\section{Goal}

We now insert the 12 exact BCC shell directions into the Class II-induced quartic matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-
\Lambda_A\,c_\alpha^2 c_\beta^2
-
\Lambda_{BC}\,c_\alpha c_\beta
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta
-
c_\alpha c_\beta
\right),
}
\label{eq:UX_master}
\end{equation}
where
\[
c_\alpha:=\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha.
\]

The purpose is to determine whether the resulting matrix is genuinely of the
four-class BCC-symmetric form
\[
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl}),
\]
or whether the anisotropy axis \(\hat n\) forces a finer orbit decomposition.

\section{Choice of shell axis and adapted frame}

Take the selected shell pair direction to be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
}
\end{equation}
Choose the adapted orthonormal frame
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_1=\frac{(1,-1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
e_2=(0,0,1),
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
}
\end{equation}

The 12 BCC directions are
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_{\rm BCC}
=
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,\pm1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}.
\end{equation}

\section{Exact orbit decomposition relative to \texorpdfstring{$\hat n$}{n}}

Relative to the chosen axis \(\hat n\), the 12 shell directions split into the five exact orbits
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{+1}=\{\hat n\},
\qquad
\mathcal O_{-1}=\{-\hat n\},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{0}
=
\left\{
\frac{(1,-1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(-1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}
\right\},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{+1/2}
=
\left\{
\frac{(1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_{-1/2}
=
\left\{
\frac{(-1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,-1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\alpha\in\left\{+1,-1,0,+\frac12,-\frac12\right\}.
}
\label{eq:c_values}
\end{equation}

This already shows that the anisotropy axis breaks the full BCC symmetry.
The shell is no longer organized only by the pairwise invariant
\[
(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2\in\{1,0,1/4\},
\]
but also by the one-body quantities \(c_\alpha,c_\beta\).

\section{Reference-row exact evaluation}

Let \(\alpha=\hat n\), so that \(c_\alpha=1\) and \(\hat k_\alpha=\hat n\).
Then
\[
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta=c_\beta.
\]
Therefore the second term in \eqref{eq:UX_master} vanishes identically:
\begin{equation}
c_\alpha c_\beta
\bigl(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta-c_\alpha c_\beta
\bigr)
=
c_\beta(c_\beta-c_\beta)=0.
\end{equation}
Hence for the reference row,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\hat n,\beta}^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A\,c_\beta^2.
}
\label{eq:reference_row}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact values are:

\subsection{Diagonal}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d^{(X)}:=U_{\hat n,\hat n}^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Opposite}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm opp}^{(X)}:=U_{\hat n,-\hat n}^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Orthogonal}
For the two orthogonal directions, \(c_\beta=0\), hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\perp}^{(X)}:=U_{\hat n,\beta_\perp}^{(X)}=0.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Oblique}
For the eight oblique directions, \(c_\beta=\pm \frac12\), hence \(c_\beta^2=\frac14\), so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm obl}^{(X)}:=U_{\hat n,\beta_{\rm obl}}^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{4}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the naive reference-row class data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A,
\qquad
U_\perp^{(X)}=0,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{4}.
}
\label{eq:naive_four_class}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate consequence for the old four-class criterion}

If one \emph{naively} inserts \eqref{eq:naive_four_class} into the old BCC-symmetric row sum
\[
R=U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl},
\]
then the \(X\)-sector contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(X)}=-4\Lambda_A.
}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(X)}-12U_d^{(X)}
=
-4\Lambda_A-12(-\Lambda_A)
=
8\Lambda_A.
}
\label{eq:naive_shift}
\end{equation}

So if \(\Lambda_A>0\), the naive four-class correction is \emph{positive}, i.e. it does not help the old
criterion \(R<12U_d\).

However, this conclusion is only heuristic, because the four-class reduction is no longer exact once the axis \(\hat n\) is fixed.

\section{Why the four-class BCC reduction fails exactly}

The key point is that \(U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}\) depends on
\[
c_\alpha,\qquad c_\beta,
\]
not only on
\[
(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2.
\]
Therefore the matrix is not determined solely by the usual BCC pair classes
\[
\text{self},\quad \text{opposite},\quad \text{orthogonal},\quad \text{oblique}.
\]

A direct counterexample is immediate:

\subsection{Row based on an orthogonal direction}
Take
\[
\hat k_\alpha=\frac{(1,-1,0)}{\sqrt2}\in \mathcal O_0.
\]
Then \(c_\alpha=0\), and hence both terms in \eqref{eq:UX_master} vanish:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=0
\qquad
\forall \beta
\quad\text{if } c_\alpha=0.
}
\label{eq:c0_row_zero}
\end{equation}

So the row corresponding to an orthogonal patch is identically zero, while the row corresponding to the axial patch \(\hat n\) is not.
This proves:

\begin{theorem}[Exact symmetry reduction theorem]
For a locked anisotropy axis \(\hat n\) chosen along a selected BCC shell direction, the Class II-induced matrix \(U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}\) is \emph{not} a full BCC-symmetric four-class matrix.
Instead, it is organized by the five one-body orbits
\[
\mathcal O_{+1},\ \mathcal O_{-1},\ \mathcal O_0,\ \mathcal O_{+1/2},\ \mathcal O_{-1/2}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:UX_master} depends explicitly on \(c_\alpha,c_\beta\), not only on
\((\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2\).
The axial row \eqref{eq:reference_row} is nontrivial, whereas the orthogonal row \eqref{eq:c0_row_zero} vanishes identically.
Therefore two directions belonging to different \(c\)-orbits cannot be related by the full BCC class symmetry.
\end{proof}

\section{Correct reduced description: orbit matrix, not class matrix}

The correct exact reduction is therefore not a \(4\times4\) class matrix but a \(5\times5\) orbit matrix,
indexed by
\[
q\in\left\{+1,-1,0,+\frac12,-\frac12\right\}.
\]

Define the orbit-averaged coupling
\begin{equation}
\overline U^{(X)}_{q,q'}
:=
\frac{1}{|\mathcal O_q|\,|\mathcal O_{q'}|}
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal O_q}
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal O_{q'}}
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}.
\label{eq:orbit_average}
\end{equation}

A direct symmetry average gives:

\begin{proposition}[Exact orbit-average formula]
For the five-orbit decomposition relative to
\(\hat n=(1,1,0)/\sqrt2\),
the mixed \(\Lambda_{BC}\)-term averages to zero on each orbit pair:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{1}{|\mathcal O_q|\,|\mathcal O_{q'}|}
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal O_q}
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal O_{q'}}
c_\alpha c_\beta
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta-c_\alpha c_\beta
\right)
=0.
}
\label{eq:BC_average_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\overline U^{(X)}_{q,q'}
=
-\Lambda_A\,q^2 q'^2.
}
\label{eq:orbit_avg_final}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

Thus the exact orbit-averaged matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\overline U^{(X)}
=
-\Lambda_A
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & 1 & 0 & 1/4 & 1/4\\
1 & 1 & 0 & 1/4 & 1/4\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\
1/4 & 1/4 & 0 & 1/16 & 1/16\\
1/4 & 1/4 & 0 & 1/16 & 1/16
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:orbit_matrix_explicit}
\end{equation}
in the orbit order
\[
(+1,-1,0,+1/2,-1/2).
\]

\section{Parity-symmetric subansatz}

A natural reduced ansatz is
\begin{equation}
r_{+1}=r_{-1}=a,
\qquad
r_0=b,
\qquad
r_{+1/2}=r_{-1/2}=c.
\label{eq:parity_ansatz}
\end{equation}
Since there are
\[
|\mathcal O_{+1}|=|\mathcal O_{-1}|=1,
\qquad
|\mathcal O_0|=2,
\qquad
|\mathcal O_{\pm1/2}|=4,
\]
the \(X\)-induced quartic energy is
\begin{align}
\mathcal F_X
&=
\frac12
\sum_{\alpha,\beta}
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)} r_\alpha r_\beta
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\Lambda_A}{2}
\left(
\sum_\alpha c_\alpha^2 r_\alpha
\right)^2
-
\frac{\Lambda_{BC}}{2}
\sum_{\alpha,\beta}
c_\alpha c_\beta
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta-c_\alpha c_\beta
\right)r_\alpha r_\beta.
\end{align}
Under the orbit-symmetric ansatz \eqref{eq:parity_ansatz}, the second term vanishes by orbit averaging, and
\[
\sum_\alpha c_\alpha^2 r_\alpha
=
1\cdot a+1\cdot a
+4\cdot \frac14 c
+4\cdot \frac14 c
=
2a+2c.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_X
=
-2\Lambda_A\,(a+c)^2.
}
\label{eq:FX_parity}
\end{equation}

This yields two exact consequences:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(c=0\) orbit is completely invisible to the \(X\)-induced quartic term;
\item the \(X\)-sector alone couples only the axial and oblique orbits through the combination \(a+c\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Most honest diagnosis}

The exact angular audit shows that the Class II sector by itself does \emph{not} restore the old full BCC-symmetric quartic competition.
Instead:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the axis-locked }X\text{-sector breaks the 12-patch problem into a 5-orbit problem.}
}
\end{equation}

Moreover, at orbit-averaged level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{BC}\text{ drops out, while }\Lambda_A\text{ only weights }c_\alpha^2.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(X\)-sector alone is too degenerate to decide the fate of the full 12-patch BCC branch.
The missing discrimination must come from:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(0)}
\quad\text{and/or additional refined geometric / mixing terms.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Nonredundant next step}

The correct next step is not to reuse the old four-class criterion.
It is to build the full orbit-reduced free energy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(a,b,c)
=
\mathcal F_0(a,b,c)
-
2\Lambda_A(a+c)^2,
}
\label{eq:next_orbit}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal F_0\) comes from the scalar/base quartic matrix \(U^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}\).

Then one must compare:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{one-patch branch}
\quad\text{vs.}\quad
\text{orbit-symmetric locked branch}
}
\end{equation}
inside this \(5\)-orbit (or parity-reduced \(3\)-parameter) system.
Only that gives the honest stabilization test for the intended branch.

\section{Final Summary}

For the locked anisotropy axis
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\]
the 12 BCC shell directions split into the five exact orbits
\[
\mathcal O_{+1},\ \mathcal O_{-1},\ \mathcal O_0,\ \mathcal O_{+1/2},\ \mathcal O_{-1/2},
\]
according to
\[
c_\alpha=\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha\in\left\{+1,-1,0,+\frac12,-\frac12\right\}.
\]

The Class II inter-patch quartic matrix
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-
\Lambda_A\,c_\alpha^2 c_\beta^2
-
\Lambda_{BC}\,c_\alpha c_\beta
\left(
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta-c_\alpha c_\beta
\right)
\]
is therefore not determined solely by the usual BCC pair classes
\[
\text{self},\ \text{opposite},\ \text{orthogonal},\ \text{oblique}.
\]

For the axial reference row \(\alpha=\hat n\), one finds
\[
U_d^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}^{(X)}=-\Lambda_A,
\qquad
U_\perp^{(X)}=0,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{4},
\]
but this does not define a genuine full BCC-symmetric four-class matrix,
because for an orthogonal row \(c_\alpha=0\) one gets
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=0
\qquad
\forall \beta.
\]

Thus the correct exact reduction is a \(5\times5\) orbit matrix, not a \(4\times4\) BCC class matrix.

After averaging over the five orbits, the mixed \(\Lambda_{BC}\)-term cancels exactly, and the orbit-averaged matrix becomes
\[
\overline U^{(X)}_{q,q'}=-\Lambda_A\,q^2 q'^2,
\qquad
q,q'\in\left\{+1,-1,0,+\frac12,-\frac12\right\}.
\]

Under the parity-symmetric orbit ansatz
\[
r_{+1}=r_{-1}=a,
\qquad
r_0=b,
\qquad
r_{+1/2}=r_{-1/2}=c,
\]
the \(X\)-induced quartic energy reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_X=-2\Lambda_A(a+c)^2.
}
\]

Hence the exact angular audit proves:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the old full-BCC four-class criterion \(R<12U_d\) is not the exact criterion once the anisotropy axis is locked;
\item the \(X\)-sector alone leaves the \(c=0\) orbit invisible and is too degenerate to decide the full 12-patch stabilization problem;
\item the honest next step is to combine this orbit-reduced \(X\)-sector with the base quartic matrix \(U^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}\) and compare one-patch vs.\ locked orbit-symmetric branches there.
\end{enumerate}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Orbit-Reduced Free Energy for \texorpdfstring{$U^{(0)}+U^{(X)}$}{U(0)+U(X)}}

\section{Goal}

The exact angular audit showed that, once the anisotropy axis is locked,
the Class II \(X\)-sector does not preserve the full BCC four-class reduction.
The correct exact reduction is the five-orbit decomposition
\[
c_\alpha=\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha\in\left\{+1,-1,0,+\frac12,-\frac12\right\}.
\]

The next task is therefore to combine the base quartic matrix \(U_{\alpha\beta}^{(0)}\)
with the \(X\)-induced matrix \(U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}\),
reduce the result to orbit variables,
and obtain the exact stabilization criterion for the locked branch.

\section{Orbit variables}

Let
\[
\mathcal O_{+1},\quad
\mathcal O_{-1},\quad
\mathcal O_{0},\quad
\mathcal O_{+1/2},\quad
\mathcal O_{-1/2}
\]
be the five exact orbits relative to the locked axis
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
\]

Impose the parity-symmetric orbit ansatz
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{+1}=r_{-1}=a,
\qquad
r_{0}=b,
\qquad
r_{+1/2}=r_{-1/2}=c.
}
\label{eq:abc_ansatz}
\end{equation}

The orbit multiplicities are
\begin{equation}
|\mathcal O_{+1}|=|\mathcal O_{-1}|=1,
\qquad
|\mathcal O_0|=2,
\qquad
|\mathcal O_{+1/2}|=|\mathcal O_{-1/2}|=4.
\label{eq:orbit_sizes}
\end{equation}

So the total shell norm is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_{\rm tot}=2a+2b+8c.
}
\label{eq:Rtot}
\end{equation}

\section{Linear growth rates}

Write the orbit-resolved quadratic coefficients as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_a:=\sigma_{+1}=\sigma_{-1},
\qquad
\sigma_b:=\sigma_0,
\qquad
\sigma_c:=\sigma_{+1/2}=\sigma_{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:sigma_abc}
\end{equation}

From the shell anisotropy
\[
\sigma_\alpha=\sigma_0+\eta P_2(c_\alpha)+\delta\sigma_\alpha,
\]
and the orbit average of the Class II linear term, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_q
=
\sigma_0+\eta P_2(q)-\Xi_A q^2,
}
\qquad
q\in\left\{1,0,\frac12\right\},
\label{eq:sigma_q_general}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\Xi_A
:=
\overline s_3
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}A
\end{equation}
is the orbit-averaged axial Class II shift.
Using
\[
P_2(1)=1,\qquad P_2(0)=-\frac12,\qquad P_2\!\left(\frac12\right)=-\frac18,
\]
this gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_a=\sigma_0+\eta-\Xi_A,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_b=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{2},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_c=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}-\frac{\Xi_A}{4}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Base quartic matrix \texorpdfstring{$U^{(0)}$}{U0}}

Assume the base scalar quartic matrix is BCC-symmetric and depends only on the standard pair classes:
\begin{equation}
U_d^{(0)},\qquad
U_{\rm opp}^{(0)},\qquad
U_{\perp}^{(0)},\qquad
U_{\rm obl}^{(0)}.
\end{equation}

For convenience define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S:=U_d^{(0)}+U_{\rm opp}^{(0)},
\qquad
T:=U_{\perp}^{(0)},
\qquad
O:=U_{\rm obl}^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:STO_def}
\end{equation}

A direct combinatorial reduction over the 12 BCC directions gives the exact base quartic energy:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_0^{(4)}(a,b,c)
=
S\,a^2
+
4T\,ab
+
16O\,ac
+
S\,b^2
+
16O\,bc
}
\nonumber\\
\qquad
+
4\bigl(S+2T+4O\bigr)c^2.
\label{eq:F0quartic}
\]

\section{Class II quartic contribution}

From the exact orbit-average audit of the \(X\)-sector,
the parity-symmetric orbit contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_X^{(4)}(a,b,c)
=
-2\Lambda_A(a+c)^2.
}
\label{eq:FXquartic}
\end{equation}

Therefore the total quartic energy is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm quartic}(a,b,c)
=
\bigl(S-2\Lambda_A\bigr)a^2
+
4T\,ab
+
\bigl(16O-4\Lambda_A\bigr)ac
}
\nonumber\\
\qquad
+
S\,b^2
+
16O\,bc
+
\bigl(4S+8T+16O-2\Lambda_A\bigr)c^2.
\label{eq:Fquartic_total}
\]

\section{Exact orbit-reduced free energy}

Including the quadratic shell-growth part, the exact parity-symmetric orbit-reduced free energy is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(a,b,c)
=
-2\sigma_a a
-2\sigma_b b
-8\sigma_c c
+
\mathcal F_{\rm quartic}(a,b,c).
}
\label{eq:Forb_abc}
\]

This is the exact reduced free energy that replaces the old naive four-class criterion.

\section{Matrix form}

Let
\begin{equation}
x:=
\begin{pmatrix}
a\\ b\\ c
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\ell:=
\begin{pmatrix}
2\sigma_a\\
2\sigma_b\\
8\sigma_c
\end{pmatrix}.
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(x)
=
-\ell^{\!\top}x
+\frac12 x^{\!\top}Kx,
}
\label{eq:Forb_matrix}
\end{equation}
with the exact symmetric matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K=
\begin{pmatrix}
2(S-2\Lambda_A) & 4T & 16O-4\Lambda_A\\[2mm]
4T & 2S & 16O\\[2mm]
16O-4\Lambda_A & 16O & 8S+16T+32O-4\Lambda_A
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:K_matrix}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact locked-branch solution}

\begin{theorem}[Exact parity-symmetric locked branch]
Assume \(K\) is positive definite.
Then the unique stationary point of \(\mathcal F_{\rm orb}\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
x_* = K^{-1}\ell.
}
\label{eq:xstar_exact}
\end{equation}
If all components of \(x_*\) are positive,
\[
a_*>0,\qquad b_*>0,\qquad c_*>0,
\]
then \(x_*\) is the exact parity-symmetric locked branch.
Its free energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm lock}
=
-\frac12\,\ell^{\!\top}K^{-1}\ell.
}
\label{eq:Flock_exact}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The functional \eqref{eq:Forb_matrix} is a strictly convex quadratic form when \(K>0\).
The unique critical point is obtained from
\[
\nabla_x \mathcal F_{\rm orb}=-\ell+Kx=0,
\]
hence \(x_*=K^{-1}\ell\).
Substituting back yields \eqref{eq:Flock_exact}.
\end{proof}

\section{Exact one-patch competitors}

The honest competitors are not just one kind of one-patch state, but three orbit types:

\subsection{Axial one-patch}
One nonzero amplitude in \(\mathcal O_{\pm1}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{1,a}(r)
=
-\sigma_a r
+
\frac12
\Bigl(U_d^{(0)}-\Lambda_A\Bigr)r^2.
}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{1,a}=\frac{\sigma_a}{U_d^{(0)}-\Lambda_A},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma_a^2}{2\left(U_d^{(0)}-\Lambda_A\right)}.
}
\label{eq:F1a}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Orthogonal one-patch}
One nonzero amplitude in \(\mathcal O_0\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{1,b}=\frac{\sigma_b}{U_d^{(0)}},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma_b^2}{2U_d^{(0)}}.
}
\label{eq:F1b}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Oblique one-patch}
One nonzero amplitude in \(\mathcal O_{\pm1/2}\).
For \(c_\alpha^2=1/4\), the exact self-coupling is
\begin{equation}
U_{\rm self,obl}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{\Lambda_A}{16}
-\frac{3\Lambda_{BC}}{16},
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{1,c}
=
\frac{\sigma_c}{U_d^{(0)}-\frac{\Lambda_A+3\Lambda_{BC}}{16}},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma_c^2}
{2\left(U_d^{(0)}-\frac{\Lambda_A+3\Lambda_{BC}}{16}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:F1c}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp stabilization criterion}

\begin{theorem}[Exact stabilization criterion]
Assume the locked branch exists, i.e.
\[
K>0,\qquad x_*=K^{-1}\ell>0.
\]
Then the parity-symmetric locked branch is energetically preferred over all one-patch competitors if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm lock}
<
\min\left\{
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:sharp_final_criterion}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

This is the exact replacement of the old naive \(R<12U_d\) criterion.

\section{Natural practical reduction: \texorpdfstring{$b=0$}{b=0} regime}

Because
\[
P_2(0)=-\frac12
\]
is the most suppressed quadratic shell weight, and because the \(X\)-sector does not directly reward the \(b\)-orbit in \eqref{eq:FXquartic},
the physically natural locked regime is often
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_*=0,
}
\label{eq:b0_regime}
\end{equation}
or at least \(b_*\ll a_*,c_*\).

Then the free energy reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{ac}(a,c)
=
-2\sigma_a a
-8\sigma_c c
+
\alpha a^2
+
\gamma ac
+
\zeta c^2,
}
\label{eq:Fac}
\]
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha:=S-2\Lambda_A,
\qquad
\gamma:=16O-4\Lambda_A,
\qquad
\zeta:=4S+8T+16O-2\Lambda_A.
}
\label{eq:agz_def}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact \texorpdfstring{$ac$}{ac} locked solution}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_{ac}:=4\alpha\zeta-\gamma^2.
}
\label{eq:Dac}
\end{equation}

If \(D_{ac}>0\), the exact stationary point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_*^{(ac)}
=
\frac{4(\zeta\sigma_a-2\gamma\sigma_c)}{D_{ac}},
}
\label{eq:aac}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_*^{(ac)}
=
\frac{2(8\alpha\sigma_c-\gamma\sigma_a)}{D_{ac}}.
}
\label{eq:cac}
\end{equation}

Its energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{ac}^{\min}
=
-\frac{4\left(
\zeta\sigma_a^2
-
4\gamma\sigma_a\sigma_c
+
16\alpha\sigma_c^2
\right)}{D_{ac}}.
}
\label{eq:Facmin}
\end{equation}

Hence the practical \(b=0\) locked branch exists if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_{ac}>0,
\qquad
\zeta\sigma_a>2\gamma\sigma_c,
\qquad
8\alpha\sigma_c>\gamma\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:ac_exist}
\end{equation}

It beats the axial and oblique one-patch branches if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{ac}^{\min}
<
\min\left\{
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:ac_win}
\end{equation}

\section{Most honest diagnosis}

At this point the structural reduction is fully closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Psi,X_i^{\,a})
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(a,b,c)
\Longrightarrow
\text{exact locked-vs-one-patch criterion}.
}
\end{equation}

What remains open is no longer the form of the criterion,
but only the insertion of the actual microscopic coefficients
\[
U_d^{(0)},\quad U_{\rm opp}^{(0)},\quad U_\perp^{(0)},\quad U_{\rm obl}^{(0)},
\quad
\Lambda_A,\quad \Lambda_{BC},\quad \Xi_A.
\]

Once these are inserted, the branch decision is immediate from
\eqref{eq:sharp_final_criterion},
or from the practical \(b=0\) formulas \eqref{eq:Facmin}--\eqref{eq:ac_win}.

\section{Final Summary}

After the exact five-orbit reduction relative to the locked axis
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\]
the full \(12\)-patch problem reduces, under the parity-symmetric ansatz,
to the three orbit variables
\[
a=r_{\pm1},
\qquad
b=r_0,
\qquad
c=r_{\pm1/2}.
\]

Let
\[
S=U_d^{(0)}+U_{\rm opp}^{(0)},
\qquad
T=U_\perp^{(0)},
\qquad
O=U_{\rm obl}^{(0)}.
\]
Then the exact orbit-reduced free energy is
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(a,b,c)
=
-2\sigma_a a
-2\sigma_b b
-8\sigma_c c
+
\bigl(S-2\Lambda_A\bigr)a^2
+
4Tab
+
\bigl(16O-4\Lambda_A\bigr)ac
+
Sb^2
+
16Obc
+
\bigl(4S+8T+16O-2\Lambda_A\bigr)c^2.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(x)
=
-\ell^{\!\top}x
+\frac12 x^{\!\top}Kx,
\]
with
\[
x=(a,b,c)^{\top},
\qquad
\ell=(2\sigma_a,2\sigma_b,8\sigma_c)^{\top},
\]
and
\[
K=
\begin{pmatrix}
2(S-2\Lambda_A) & 4T & 16O-4\Lambda_A\\
4T & 2S & 16O\\
16O-4\Lambda_A & 16O & 8S+16T+32O-4\Lambda_A
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If \(K>0\), the exact locked branch is
\[
x_*=K^{-1}\ell,
\]
with energy
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm lock}
=
-\frac12 \ell^{\!\top}K^{-1}\ell.
}
\]

The one-patch competitors are:

\[
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma_a^2}{2(U_d^{(0)}-\Lambda_A)},
\]
\[
\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma_b^2}{2U_d^{(0)}},
\]
\[
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma_c^2}
{2\left(U_d^{(0)}-\frac{\Lambda_A+3\Lambda_{BC}}{16}\right)}.
\]

Therefore the exact stabilization criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm lock}
<
\min\left\{
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
\right\}.
}
\]

In the natural \(b=0\) regime, define
\[
\alpha=S-2\Lambda_A,
\qquad
\gamma=16O-4\Lambda_A,
\qquad
\zeta=4S+8T+16O-2\Lambda_A,
\]
\[
D_{ac}=4\alpha\zeta-\gamma^2.
\]
Then the locked \(ac\)-branch is
\[
a_*^{(ac)}
=
\frac{4(\zeta\sigma_a-2\gamma\sigma_c)}{D_{ac}},
\qquad
c_*^{(ac)}
=
\frac{2(8\alpha\sigma_c-\gamma\sigma_a)}{D_{ac}},
\]
with energy
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{ac}^{\min}
=
-\frac{4\left(
\zeta\sigma_a^2
-
4\gamma\sigma_a\sigma_c
+
16\alpha\sigma_c^2
\right)}{D_{ac}}.
}
\]

Hence the structure is now fully reduced:
the only remaining open task is to insert the actual microscopic coefficients
\[
U_d^{(0)},\ U_{\rm opp}^{(0)},\ U_\perp^{(0)},\ U_{\rm obl}^{(0)},
\ \Lambda_A,\ \Lambda_{BC},\ \Xi_A,
\]
and evaluate the above inequalities numerically.

\section{Actual Base Shell Kernel Extracted from the Uploaded Locked 12-Mode BCC Branch}

\section{What is actually available from the uploaded branch data}

The uploaded locked-branch notes fix three facts:

Therefore the object that is actually extracted from the current uploaded branch is not yet the full bare quartic matrix \(U^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}\), but the shell-level base kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}
:=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(Q_\alpha-Q_\beta).

\label{eq:K0_def}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal scalar locked-core kernel}

Under the current minimal scalar locked core,
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(0)=12uA^2,
\qquad
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(Q)=4uA^2
\quad(Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}),

and no other first-shell Fourier channels are explicitly present in the uploaded branch data.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^{(0)}_{\alpha\beta}
=

+
4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_{\{Q_\alpha-Q_\beta\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\}}.
}
\label{eq:K0_minimal}
\end{equation}

This is the actual base kernel presently available from the working branch.

\section{Locked-axis orbit decomposition}

Fix the locked axis
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
\]
Then the 12 BCC directions split into the five exact orbits
\[
\mathcal O_{+1},\quad
\mathcal O_{-1},\quad
\mathcal O_0,\quad
\mathcal O_{+1/2},\quad
\mathcal O_{-1/2}.

Impose the parity-symmetric intensity ansatz
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{+1}=r_{-1}=a,
\qquad
r_0=b,
\qquad
r_{+1/2}=r_{-1/2}=c.
}
\label{eq:abc_ansatz_again}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact orbit action of the base kernel}

For a representative axial patch \(Q_\alpha\in\mathcal O_{+1}\), one finds
\[
Q_\alpha-Q_\beta\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
Q_\beta\in \mathcal O_{+1/2}.

Hence
\begin{equation}

=

+
16uA^2\,c.

\label{eq:K0_axial}

For a representative opposite axial patch \(Q_\alpha\in\mathcal O_{-1}\),
\begin{equation}

(K^{(0)}r)_{-1}
=
12uA^2\,a
+
16uA^2\,c.
}
\label{eq:K0_minusaxial}
\end{equation}

For a representative orthogonal patch \(Q_\alpha\in\mathcal O_0\), the shell-difference condition hits exactly one member of each oblique-sign orbit, so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(K^{(0)}r)_0
=
12uA^2\,b
+
16uA^2\,c.
}
\label{eq:K0_orth}
\end{equation}

For a representative oblique patch \(Q_\alpha\in\mathcal O_{+1/2}\), the shell-difference condition hits:
\[
1 \text{ axial patch},\qquad
1 \text{ orthogonal patch},\qquad
4 \text{ same-sign oblique/diagonal-weighted entries},\qquad
1 \text{ opposite-sign oblique patch}.
\]
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(K^{(0)}r)_{+1/2}
=
4uA^2\,a
+
4uA^2\,b
+
20uA^2\,c.
}
\label{eq:K0_oblplus}
\end{equation}
By parity,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(K^{(0)}r)_{-1/2}
=
4uA^2\,a
+
4uA^2\,b
+
20uA^2\,c.
}
\label{eq:K0_oblminus}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact parity-reduced quadratic form}

The orbit-reduced base quadratic form is therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F^{(0)}_{\mathrm{base}}(a,b,c)
=

+

+

+

\label{eq:F0base_abc}

Equivalently, in matrix form,

x=(a,b,c)^\top,

with

24uA^2 & 0 & 32uA^2\\
0 & 24uA^2 & 32uA^2\\
32uA^2 & 32uA^2 & 160uA^2
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:K0_matrix}
\end{equation}

\section{Combination with the Class II \texorpdfstring{$X$}{X}-sector}

From the previous exact orbit audit, the parity-symmetric \(X\)-sector contributes

+
32uA^2\,bc
+

\begin{equation}

32uA^2\,b
+
2(80uA^2-2\Lambda_A)c.

\section{Most honest consequence}

At this point, the actual uploaded branch data determine the scalar base kernel completely enough to replace the earlier surrogate \(S,T,O\)-parametrization by the explicit matrix \eqref{eq:K0_matrix}.

Thus the true currently closed reduced problem is

(\Psi,X)\text{-working branch}

with \(\mathcal F_{\mathrm{work}}\) given explicitly by \eqref{eq:Fwork_expanded}.

What still remains open is no longer the scalar base kernel.
It is the insertion of the actual branch values of

\section{Minimal Actual Working-Branch Theorem}

\section{Actual coefficients already fixed by the uploaded branch}

From the uploaded locked-branch files, the minimal scalar-only locked core gives
\begin{equation}

\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(0)=12uA^2,
\qquad
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)=4uA^2,

and the full 12-mode BCC combinatorics gives

Therefore it is natural to define the actual scalar Bragg scale
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_0:=4uA^2.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
12uA^2=3m_0.
\]

\section{Actual reduced free energy in terms of \texorpdfstring{$m_0$}{m0}}

The parity-symmetric orbit-reduced working free energy becomes
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{work}}(a,b,c)
&=
-2\sigma_a a
-2\sigma_b b
-8\sigma_c c
+
(3m_0-2\Lambda_A)a^2
+

}
\nonumber\\

+
(8m_0-4\Lambda_A)ac
+
8m_0\,bc
+
(20m_0-2\Lambda_A)c^2 .
}
\label{eq:Fwork_m0}
\end{align}

The exact stationarity equations are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0
=
-2\sigma_a
+
2(3m_0-2\Lambda_A)a
+
(8m_0-4\Lambda_A)c,

\label{eq:stat_a_m0}

\begin{equation}

=

+

+

\label{eq:stat_b_m0}

=

+

+
8m_0\,b
+
2(20m_0-2\Lambda_A)c.

\label{eq:stat_c_m0}

\section{Minimal actual closure ansatz}

At the current sharpest honestly closed level, the uploaded files fix the scalar base shell core,
but do not yet separately extract the orbit-split linear coefficients
\[
\sigma_a,\qquad \sigma_b,\qquad \sigma_c.
\]
Therefore the minimal actual working-branch closure is to impose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_a=\sigma_b=\sigma_c=:\sigma.
}
\label{eq:minimal_sigma_equal}
\end{equation}

This is the strongest closed reduction available before the explicit orbit-split transport extraction is finished.

\section{Exact locked-branch solution}

Under \eqref{eq:minimal_sigma_equal}, the unique stationary point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_*
=
\frac{\sigma(6m_0+5\Lambda_A)}
{m_0(42m_0-29\Lambda_A)},
}
\label{eq:a_star_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_*
=
\frac{3\sigma(2m_0-\Lambda_A)}
{m_0(42m_0-29\Lambda_A)},
}
\label{eq:b_star_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_*
=
\frac{\sigma(6m_0-5\Lambda_A)}
{m_0(42m_0-29\Lambda_A)}.
}
\label{eq:c_star_final}
\end{equation}

The locked-branch energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{lock}}^{\min}
=
-\frac{18\sigma^2(2m_0-\Lambda_A)}
{m_0(42m_0-29\Lambda_A)}.
}
\label{eq:Flock_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Existence and positivity conditions}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal actual locked branch]
Assume
\[
\sigma>0.
\]
Then the stationary point \eqref{eq:a_star_final}--\eqref{eq:c_star_final} is positive and therefore defines a genuine locked orbit branch provided
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<\Lambda_A<\frac{6}{5}m_0.
}
\label{eq:LA_window}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The common denominator is
\[
m_0(42m_0-29\Lambda_A),
\]
which is positive if \(\Lambda_A<42m_0/29\).
The numerators are
\[
6m_0+5\Lambda_A>0,
\qquad
2m_0-\Lambda_A,
\qquad
6m_0-5\Lambda_A.
\]
So positivity of all three components requires
\[
2m_0-\Lambda_A>0,
\qquad
6m_0-5\Lambda_A>0.
\]
The stronger bound is exactly
\[
\Lambda_A<\frac65 m_0.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{One-patch competitors}

The axial one-patch branch has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma^2}{2(3m_0-\Lambda_A)}.
}
\label{eq:F1a_m0}
\end{equation}

The orthogonal one-patch branch has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma^2}{6m_0}.
}
\label{eq:F1b_m0}
\end{equation}

The oblique one-patch branch has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma^2}
{2\left(3m_0-\frac{\Lambda_A+3\Lambda_{BC}}{16}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:F1c_m0}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp minimal sufficient stabilization theorem}

In the minimal \(X\)-sector reduction where the orbit-averaged \(\Lambda_{BC}\) contribution is absent at leading locked level,
we set
\[
\Lambda_{BC}=0
\]
for the first actual working-branch test.

Then:

\begin{theorem}[Minimal actual sufficient stabilization]
Assume
\[
\sigma>0,
\qquad
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65 m_0,
\qquad
\Lambda_{BC}=0.
\]
Then the locked orbit branch exists and beats all one-patch competitors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{lock}}^{\min}
<
\min\left\{
\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min},
\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:minimal_stabilization}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Define
\[
x:=\frac{\Lambda_A}{m_0}.
\]
Then \(0<x<6/5\).

A direct subtraction gives
\begin{equation}
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{lock}}^{\min}-\mathcal F_{1,a}^{\min}
=
-\frac{\sigma^2(36x^2-151x+174)}
{2m_0(x-3)(29x-42)}.
\end{equation}
Since \(36x^2-151x+174>0\) for all real \(x\), and in the range \(0<x<6/5\) one has
\[
x-3<0,\qquad 29x-42<0,
\]
the denominator is positive, so the whole expression is negative.

Similarly,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{lock}}^{\min}-\mathcal F_{1,b}^{\min}
=
\frac{\sigma^2(174-79x)}
{6m_0(29x-42)}<0,
\end{equation}
because \(174-79x>0\) in the same range while \(29x-42<0\).

Finally, for \(\Lambda_{BC}=0\),
\begin{equation}
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{lock}}^{\min}-\mathcal F_{1,c}^{\min}
=
-\frac{2\sigma^2(18x^2-668x+1392)}
{m_0(x-48)(29x-42)}<0,
\end{equation}
because \(18x^2-668x+1392>0\) throughout \(0<x<6/5\), while
\[
x-48<0,\qquad 29x-42<0.
\]
Hence all three differences are negative.
\end{proof}

\section{Interpretation}

The uploaded actual branch data already close the base scalar shell core strongly enough that the true minimal working-branch decision reduces to a single interval test:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65 m_0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{locked orbit branch wins}.
}
\label{eq:single_interval_test}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using \(m_0=4uA^2\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<\Lambda_A<\frac{24}{5}uA^2.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Most honest status}

At this point, the actual uploaded branch data are sufficient to reduce the stabilization problem to the single coefficient ratio
\[
\Lambda_A/m_0.
\]

What is still not yet numerically extracted from the uploaded files is the literal value of \(\Lambda_A\).
Also, the exact orbit-split linear coefficients
\[
\sigma_a,\ \sigma_b,\ \sigma_c
\]
have not yet been separately computed; the present theorem uses the strongest honest minimal closure
\[
\sigma_a=\sigma_b=\sigma_c=\sigma.
\]

So the exact current status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{base shell core: actually extracted,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{minimal locked-branch theorem: actually closed,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

}

\section{Actual-Branch Compression of \texorpdfstring{$\Lambda_A$}{LambdaA}}

\section{Goal}

We combine the uploaded actual working-branch data with the previously derived orbit-reduced shell theory
and compress the remaining stabilization coefficient \(\Lambda_A\) into directly interpretable branch quantities.

To avoid symbol collision, we denote:

\begin{itemize}
\item by \(\mathcal A\): the scalar locked-core shell amplitude appearing in
\[
m_0=4u\mathcal A^2;
\]
\item by \(\mathcal A_\parallel\): the Class II axial invariant coefficient appearing in the shell witness shift.
\end{itemize}

\section{Step 1: Actual scalar shell scale from the uploaded locked core}

From the uploaded minimal scalar-only locked core, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)=\omega_B(k_*)+12u\mathcal A^2,
\qquad
B_{z_0}(0)=4u\mathcal A^2.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the actual scalar Bragg scale is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_0:=4u\mathcal A^2.
}
\label{eq:m0_actual}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
12u\mathcal A^2=3m_0.
\end{equation}

\section{Step 2: Actual axial witness shift from the Class II mediator}

From the uploaded Class II corrected microscopic matching theorem,
the axial witness shift is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta W_\parallel
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal A_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:dW_actual}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A_\parallel
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\lambda g_X}\,\delta W_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:Apar_from_dW}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 3: Quartic coefficient generated by heavy-mediator elimination}

In the orbit-reduced shell theory derived earlier, the axial quartic coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_A
=
\chi_3
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
\mathcal A_\parallel^2,
}
\label{eq:LambdaA_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\chi_3>0\) is the positive susceptibility of the heavy shell mediator in the axial channel.

Substituting \eqref{eq:Apar_from_dW} into \eqref{eq:LambdaA_def}, one obtains the exact compressed formula
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_A
=
\chi_3\,q_0^4\,(\delta W_\parallel)^2.
}
\label{eq:LambdaA_compressed}
\end{equation}

This is the key reduction.

\section{Step 4: Immediate sign theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Actual sign closure for the axial quartic coefficient]
Assume the heavy shell susceptibility satisfies
\[
\chi_3>0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta W_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Lambda_A>0.
}
\end{equation}
Moreover,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_A=0
\iff
\delta W_\parallel=0.
}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:LambdaA_compressed} gives
\[
\Lambda_A=\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2.
\]
Since \(q_0^4>0\), \((\delta W_\parallel)^2\ge0\), and \(\chi_3>0\), the conclusion follows immediately.
\end{proof}

\section{Step 5: Insert into the minimal actual locked-branch theorem}

The previously derived minimal actual locked-branch window is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65\,m_0.
}
\label{eq:min_window}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:m0_actual} and \eqref{eq:LambdaA_compressed}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<
\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
<
\frac65\,4u\mathcal A^2.
}
\label{eq:window_compressed}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<
\frac{\Lambda_A}{m_0}
=
\frac{\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}{4u\mathcal A^2}
<
\frac65.
}
\label{eq:ratio_compressed}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire locked-vs-one-patch stabilization problem is reduced to the single ratio
\[
\frac{\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}{4u\mathcal A^2}.
\]

\section{Step 6: Relation to the uploaded one-mediator anisotropy scale}

The uploaded one-mediator working-branch notes also show that the one-mediator anisotropy scale is naturally heavy-suppressed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{II}}
=
\frac{g_X^2\mathcal A^3|G_*|^2}{8|Z|M_X^2},
}
\end{equation}
and that, in the natural heavy-mediator regime,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{II}}<\rho_{12}
}
\end{equation}
is the generic ordering.

Therefore the uploaded branch data strongly support the qualitative expectation that
the Class II contribution is parametrically suppressed by inverse powers of \(M_X^2\).
Since \(\Lambda_A\) is quadratic in the mediator-induced axial insertion,
its natural scale is even smaller:
\[
\Lambda_A \sim O(M_X^{-4})
\]
relative to unsuppressed scalar-core scales.

This makes it natural, though not yet numerically proved, that the upper bound
\[
\Lambda_A<\frac65\,m_0
\]
should hold in the genuine heavy-mediator regime.

\section{Step 7: What is now actually closed}

The following are now closed at the actual working-branch level:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the scalar shell core scale
\[
m_0=4u\mathcal A^2;
\]
\item the axial mediator-induced witness shift
\[
\delta W_\parallel
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\mathcal A_\parallel;
\]
\item the exact compressed quartic coefficient
\[
\Lambda_A=\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2;
\]
\item the sign theorem
\[
\delta W_\parallel\neq0 \Longrightarrow \Lambda_A>0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Step 8: What still remains open}

The only genuinely remaining scalar quantity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3,
}
\end{equation}
or equivalently the single ratio
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}{4u\mathcal A^2}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the final actual branch decision is no longer a multi-parameter structural problem.
It is a one-number insertion problem.

\section{Final actual-branch theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal actual working-branch compression theorem]
Using the uploaded locked-core branch data and the orbit-reduced Class II shell theory,
the locked-branch stabilization criterion
\[
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65\,m_0
\]
is exactly equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<
\frac{\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}{4u\mathcal A^2}
<
\frac65.
}
\end{equation}
Hence the full actual working-branch stabilization problem is compressed to a single unresolved number, namely \(\chi_3\).
\end{theorem}

\section{Final Summary}

The uploaded actual working-branch data already fix the scalar shell scale
\[
\boxed{
m_0=4u\mathcal A^2.
}
\]

They also fix the Class II axial witness shift
\[
\boxed{
\delta W_\parallel
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal A_\parallel.
}
\]

Using the previously derived orbit-reduced shell theory, the axial quartic stabilization coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_A
=
\chi_3
\left(
\frac{\lambda g_X q_0^2}{M_X^2}
\right)^2
\mathcal A_\parallel^2
=
\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2.
}
\]

Therefore:

\delta W_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_A>0
\qquad
(\chi_3>0).
}
\]

The minimal actual locked-branch condition
\[
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65\,m_0
\]
becomes
\[
\boxed{
0<
\frac{\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}{4u\mathcal A^2}
<
\frac65.
}
\]

Hence the full actual working-branch stabilization problem is no longer a many-parameter structural problem.
It is reduced to the single unresolved scalar quantity
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3.

So the present status is:

\boxed{
m_0\ \text{closed},\qquad

\Lambda_A\ \text{compressed},\qquad
\text{final open slot}=\chi_3.
}

\section{Heavy-Shell Susceptibility Interpretation of \texorpdfstring{$\chi_3$}{chi3}}

\section{Goal}

The remaining scalar quantity in the minimal actual working-branch theorem is
\[
\chi_3,
\]
appearing through
\[
\Lambda_A=\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2.
\]
The goal is to identify \(\chi_3\) as an actual heavy-shell susceptibility and reduce the final branch criterion to a finite resolvent inequality.

\section{Step 1: Exact heavy-shell meaning of \texorpdfstring{$\chi_3$}{chi3}}

Let \(\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\) be the heavy-sector operator at the locked background, and let
\[
|v_\parallel\rangle
\]
denote the projected heavy source vector generated by the longitudinal axial insertion.
Then the exact second-order heavy-mediated axial quartic correction has the standard Schur-resolvent form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3
=
\langle v_\parallel,(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}v_\parallel\rangle
=
\sum_\alpha \frac{|\mathcal E_{\parallel\alpha}|^2}{E_\alpha},
}
\label{eq:chi3_exact}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}|\chi_\alpha\rangle=E_\alpha|\chi_\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
|v_\parallel\rangle=\sum_\alpha \mathcal E_{\parallel\alpha}|\chi_\alpha\rangle.
\]

Thus \(\chi_3\) is not an abstract constant:
it is the heavy-shell susceptibility of the axial source.

\section{Step 2: Comparison with the uploaded explicit heavy-source theorem}

The uploaded heavy-source notes already contain the exact same structure in the pure-even channel:
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
=
\sum_\alpha \frac{|\mathcal E_{+\alpha}^{(z_0)}|^2}{E_\alpha}.
\]
Hence the axial channel is structurally of the same type:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3
\ \text{is the longitudinal analogue of}\ 
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}.
}
\label{eq:chi3_as_Sdiag}
\end{equation}

So the remaining job is not conceptual.
It is only the actual insertion of the axial source vector \(v_\parallel\).

\section{Step 3: Rigorous heavy-gap upper bound}

Assume the heavy spectrum obeys
\[
E_\alpha\ge \Delta_H>0.
\]
Then from \eqref{eq:chi3_exact},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3
\le
\frac{1}{\Delta_H}\|v_\parallel\|^2.
}
\label{eq:chi3_gap_bound}
\end{equation}

This is the exact longitudinal analogue of the uploaded bound
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}\le \frac{\|v_E^{(+)}\|^2}{\Delta_H}.
\]

Therefore the quartic stabilization coefficient satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_A
=
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\chi_3
\le
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaA_gap_bound}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 4: Source-aligned \texorpdfstring{$N=1$}{N=1} variational realization}

Choose the \(N=1\) heavy trial space aligned with the axial source vector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\chi_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{trial}}\rangle
=
\frac{|v_\parallel\rangle}{\|v_\parallel\|}.
}
\end{equation}
Define the corresponding variational heavy energy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}
:=
\langle \chi_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{trial}}|\mathbb O_H^{(0)}|\chi_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{trial}}\rangle.
}
\end{equation}

Then the source-aligned one-mode approximation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}
=
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}.
}
\label{eq:chi3_N1}
\end{equation}

Hence the corresponding approximate quartic coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_A^{(1)}
=
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaA_N1}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 5: Final locked-branch sufficient criterion}

The minimal actual locked-branch theorem required
\[
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65\,m_0.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:LambdaA_gap_bound}, a rigorous sufficient condition is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac65\,m_0.

\label{eq:final_sufficient_gap}

Using the \(N=1\) variational realization instead gives the finite working criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0<
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}
<
\frac65\,m_0.
}
\label{eq:final_sufficient_N1}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 6: Insert the actual scalar shell scale}

From the uploaded locked scalar core,
\[

Hence \eqref{eq:final_sufficient_gap} becomes

\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.

\section{Step 7: Honest final status}

At this point, the branch decision is no longer controlled by the abstract scalar \(\chi_3\).
It is controlled by the explicit heavy-source data:
\[
\|v_\parallel\|^2,
\qquad
\Delta_H,
\qquad
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}.

So the full actual working-branch stabilization problem is reduced to one finite heavy-source insertion problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }v_\parallel\text{ and either }\Delta_H\text{ or }E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Heavy-susceptibility compression theorem]
The remaining coefficient \(\chi_3\) in the minimal actual working-branch theorem is exactly the axial heavy-shell susceptibility
\[
\chi_3=\langle v_\parallel,(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}v_\parallel\rangle.

It admits:
\[
\chi_3^{(1)}=\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}},

q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac65\,m_0,

and a finite working test is
\[
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}
<
\frac65\,m_0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\section{Final Summary}

The last unresolved scalar coefficient
\[
\chi_3

This admits two practical realizations:

\section{Actual axial heavy-source definition}

\section{Heavy Schur template}

Choose the heavy basis \(\{\chi_\alpha\}\subset\mathcal H_H\) diagonalizing the reference heavy block:
\[
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\chi_\alpha=E_\alpha\chi_\alpha,
\qquad
E_\alpha\ge \Delta_H>0.
\]
Then the exact second-order heavy correction has the universal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}^{(2)})_{ab}
=
-\sum_\alpha
\frac{K_{a\alpha}\overline{K_{b\alpha}}}{E_\alpha},
\qquad
K_{a\alpha}=\langle a|V_{\rm shell}(0)|\chi_\alpha\rangle.
}
\label{eq:heavy_schur_template_axial}
\end{equation}

\section{Primitive longitudinal source}

In the concrete Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the longitudinal channel is sourced by the primitive \(OO\)-block transport seed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Vparallel_prim_actual}
\end{equation}

Let the corresponding shell-level longitudinal source operator be denoted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_\parallel.
}
\end{equation}
This is the axial analogue of the even-channel source operator \(\mathcal O_E\).

\section{Definition of the axial heavy source vector}

The natural exact axial heavy source vector is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|v_\parallel\rangle
:=
\Pi_H\,\mathcal O_\parallel\,|G_+,z_0\rangle.
}
\label{eq:vparallel_def}
\end{equation}

This is not an additional assumption; it is the exact axial analogue of the already-used even-channel definition
\[
|v_E\rangle=\Pi_H\mathcal O_E|G_+,z_0\rangle.
\]

\section{Exact susceptibility}

With \eqref{eq:vparallel_def}, the remaining axial susceptibility is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3
=
\langle v_\parallel,(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}v_\parallel\rangle
=
\sum_\alpha \frac{|\mathcal E_{\parallel\alpha}|^2}{E_\alpha},
}
\label{eq:chi3_exact_axial}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal E_{\parallel\alpha}
:=
\langle \chi_\alpha|v_\parallel\rangle.
\]

\section{Source-aligned \(N=1\) realization}

Choose the trial vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\chi_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{trial}}\rangle
=
\frac{|v_\parallel\rangle}{\|v_\parallel\|}.
}
\label{eq:trial_axial}
\end{equation}
Then the one-mode variational heavy energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}
=
\langle \chi_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{trial}}|
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}
|\chi_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{trial}}\rangle,
}
\label{eq:E1var_axial}
\end{equation}
and the corresponding finite working approximation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}
=
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}.
}
\label{eq:chi3_1_axial}
\end{equation}

\section{Gap bound}

Since \(E_\alpha\ge \Delta_H>0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_3
\le
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}.
}
\label{eq:chi3_gap_axial}
\end{equation}

\section{Insertion into the locked-branch criterion}

From the previous compression,
\[
\Lambda_A=\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2,
\qquad
m_0=4u\mathcal A^2.
\]
Hence the rigorous sufficient locked-branch condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.
}
\label{eq:final_gap_test_axial}
\end{equation}

Likewise the \(N=1\) working test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.
}
\label{eq:final_N1_test_axial}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining coefficient \(\chi_3\) is the axial heavy-shell susceptibility.

Its exact definition is
\[
\boxed{
|v_\parallel\rangle
=
\Pi_H\mathcal O_\parallel|G_+,z_0\rangle,
}
\]
where \(\mathcal O_\parallel\) is the shell-level source operator induced by the primitive longitudinal transport seed
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3
=
\langle v_\parallel,(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}v_\parallel\rangle
=
\sum_\alpha \frac{|\mathcal E_{\parallel\alpha}|^2}{E_\alpha}.
}
\]

The source-aligned one-mode realization is
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}
=
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}},
\qquad
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}
=
\left\langle
\frac{v_\parallel}{\|v_\parallel\|},
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}
\frac{v_\parallel}{\|v_\parallel\|}
\right\rangle.
}
\]

The rigorous heavy-gap bound is
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3
\le
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}.
}
\]

Hence the final sufficient locked-branch criterion is
\[
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2,
}
\]
and the practical \(N=1\) working test is
\[
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.
}
\]

Thus the final actual working-branch problem is reduced to the finite computation of
\[
\boxed{
\|v_\parallel\|^2,
\qquad
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}},
\qquad
\Delta_H.
}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$\|v_\parallel\|^2$}{||vparallel||^2} and \texorpdfstring{$E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}$}{Eparallel,1var}}

\section{Goal}

We now evaluate the remaining finite heavy-source data for the primitive longitudinal channel.

The actual projected primitive seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{proj}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Vpar_proj_input}
\end{equation}

We work in the same source-aligned \(N=1\) variational closure already used in the pure-even channel,
but now for the axial source.

\section{1. Canonical source vector}

Take the minimal shell test mode
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\psi(x)=e^{ik_* x_\parallel}\,\xi,
\qquad
\xi^\dagger\xi=1,
\qquad
\xi^\dagger\sigma_3^\dagger\sigma_3\xi=1.
}
\label{eq:min_shell_test}
\end{equation}

The first-order transport operator acts as
\[
-iV^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{proj}}\partial_\mu.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal O_\parallel \psi
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,k_*\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\psi.
}
\label{eq:Opar_psi}
\end{equation}

Therefore the axial heavy source vector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|v_\parallel\rangle
=
\Pi_H\,\mathcal O_\parallel\,|G_+,z_0\rangle,
}
\end{equation}
and, at the same leading order as in the pure-even source calculation, the heavy projection does not change the spatial norm:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|v_\parallel\|^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 k_*^2}{4}
\int d^3x\,\theta'(\xi)^6.
}
\label{eq:vpar_norm_start}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Sech defect profile}

Take the standard localized defect profile
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\operatorname{sech}(\kappa\xi).
}
\label{eq:theta_sech}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)
=
-\theta_0\kappa\,
\operatorname{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
}
\label{eq:theta_prime_sech}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)^6
=
\theta_0^6\kappa^6
\operatorname{sech}^6(\kappa\xi)\tanh^6(\kappa\xi).
\end{equation}

Factorizing the transverse area \(A_\perp\),
\begin{equation}
\|v_\parallel\|^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 k_*^2}{4}\,
A_\perp
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,\theta'(\xi)^6.
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact norm integral}

Set \(s=\kappa\xi\). Then
\begin{equation}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,\theta'(\xi)^6
=
\theta_0^6\kappa^5
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}ds\,
\operatorname{sech}^6(s)\tanh^6(s).
\end{equation}

Now use \(u=\tanh s\), so \(du=(1-u^2)\,ds\), and
\[
\operatorname{sech}^2 s = 1-u^2.
\]
Hence
\begin{align}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\operatorname{sech}^6(s)\tanh^6(s)\,ds
&=
\int_{-1}^{1}u^6(1-u^2)^2\,du
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac{16}{693}.
\end{align}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,\theta'(\xi)^6
=
\frac{16}{693}\,\theta_0^6\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:theta6_exact}
\end{equation}

Substituting into \eqref{eq:vpar_norm_start},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|v_\parallel\|^2
=
\frac{4}{693}\,
\lambda_c^2 k_*^2
A_\perp
\theta_0^6\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:vpar_norm_final}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Source-aligned variational heavy energy}

Take the same heavy operator model as in the explicit even-channel variational audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}
=
M_H^2
-
Z\nabla^2
+
Y\nabla^4.
}
\label{eq:OH0}
\end{equation}

For the axial source, the profile factor is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel(x)
=
f_\parallel(\xi)e^{ik_*x_\parallel},
\qquad
f_\parallel(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:vpar_factorized}
\end{equation}

Since the overall factor \(\lambda_c/2\) cancels in the Rayleigh quotient,
the variational energy depends only on the shape
\[
f(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)^3.
\]

\section{5. Exact transverse moment ratios for \texorpdfstring{$f(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)^3$}{f=theta' cubed}}

Write again \(s=\kappa\xi\), and define
\[
g(s):=\operatorname{sech}^3(s)\tanh^3(s),
\qquad
f(\xi)=\theta_0^3\kappa^3 g(\kappa\xi).
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\frac{\int |f'(\xi)|^2\,d\xi}{\int |f(\xi)|^2\,d\xi}
=
\kappa^2
\frac{\int |g'(s)|^2\,ds}{\int |g(s)|^2\,ds}.
\end{equation}

The denominator is
\[
\int |g|^2 ds
=
\int_{-1}^1 u^6(1-u^2)^2\,du
=
\frac{16}{693}.
\]

A direct computation gives
\[
g'(s)^2
\leadsto
9u^4(1-u^2)^2(2u^2-1)^2,
\]
hence
\[
\int |g'|^2 ds
=
9\int_{-1}^1 u^4(1-u^2)^2(2u^2-1)^2\,du
=
\frac{368}{5005}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_2^{(\parallel)}
:=
\frac{\int |f'|^2}{\int |f|^2}
=
\frac{207}{65}\,\kappa^2.
}
\label{eq:mu2_parallel}
\end{equation}

Similarly,
\[
\mu_4^{(\parallel)}
:=
\frac{\int |f''|^2}{\int |f|^2}
=
\frac{2529}{65}\,\kappa^4.
\]
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_4^{(\parallel)}
=
\frac{2529}{65}\,\kappa^4.
}
\label{eq:mu4_parallel}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact \(N=1\) source-aligned variational energy}

For the factorized mode \(f_\parallel(\xi)e^{ik_*x_\parallel}\), the source-aligned \(N=1\) Rayleigh quotient becomes
\begin{align}
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}
&=
M_H^2
+
Z\Bigl(k_*^2+\mu_2^{(\parallel)}\Bigr)
+
Y\Bigl(k_*^4+2k_*^2\mu_2^{(\parallel)}+\mu_4^{(\parallel)}\Bigr).
\end{align}

Using \eqref{eq:mu2_parallel} and \eqref{eq:mu4_parallel},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}
=
M_H^2
+
Z\left(
k_*^2+\frac{207}{65}\kappa^2
\right)
+
Y\left(
k_*^4+\frac{414}{65}k_*^2\kappa^2+\frac{2529}{65}\kappa^4
\right).
}
\label{eq:E1var_parallel_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Explicit one-mode axial susceptibility}
